â”‚ Now that I have the plugin architecture analysis, I can see the patterns clearly:

1. **Plugin Setup Pattern**: Three-phase approach (setup â†’ orchestrator storage â†’ register watchers)
2. **Existing Examples**:
   - autoplayPlugin: Visibility-based control using IntersectionObserver
   - virtualScrollPlugin: Batch intersection management
   - relationshipsPlugin: RAF-based continuous updates

The user's initial API proposal has two modes:
- **threshold mode**: Play animation once when scroll threshold reached (like autoplayPlugin)
- **scrub mode**: Animation progress linked to scroll position (like a timeline scrubber)

Key insight: This needs to be TWO different features:
1. **Scroll Triggers**: When to start/stop animations based on scroll position
2. **Scroll Scrubbing**: Sync animation progress to scroll progress

Let me refine the API based on the research...   â”‚

â”‚ API Design Refinement based on research:

The user's original API had:
```typescript
scroll: {
  mode: 'threshold' | 'scrub',
  threshold: 0.25,
  trigger: 'enter' | 'exit' | 'both',
  start: 0,
  end: 1,
  container: window | HTMLElement,
  animation: { keyframes: [...] }
}
```

But looking at the plugin architecture, I see issues:
1. The `animation` property shouldn't be in scroll options - that's handled by webAnimationPlugin
2. The scroll plugin should COORDINATE with webAnimationPlugin, not replace it
3. Need to support both IntersectionObserver (for triggers) and continuous scroll tracking (for scrubbing)

Better API structure:
```typescript
scroll: {
  // TRIGGER MODE: When to play/pause animation
  trigger?: {
    element?: HTMLElement,  // Element to observe (default: target)
    start: string | number, // 'top center', '50%', 200px
    end?: string | number,  // When to end (for scrub mode)
    threshold?: number,     // Intersection threshold (0-1)
    onEnter?: () => void,
    onLeave?: () => void,
    onEnterBack?: () => void,
    onLeaveBack?: () => void
  },
  
  // SCRUB MODE: Sync animation to scroll
  scrub?: boolean | number, // true or smooth factor (0-1)
  
  // SCROLL CONTAINER
  container?: HTMLElement | Window,
  
  // PERFORMANCE
  throttle?: number,  // Throttle scroll events (ms)
  
  // DEBUG
  markers?: boolean  // Show visual markers for start/end
}
```

This separates concerns better.   â”‚

â”‚ Implementation Strategy:

Based on the plugin patterns I've seen, the scroll plugin needs:

1. **Setup Phase** (setup() method):
   - Initialize useScroll from VueUse for scroll position tracking
   - Set up scroll progress calculation (0-1 based on start/end points)
   - Create IntersectionObserver if trigger mode is used
   - Store scroll state in sharedData for other plugins

2. **Watcher Phase** (registerWatchers() method):
   - Watch scroll progress and update animation currentTime if scrub mode
   - Watch intersection state and call play()/pause() if trigger mode
   - Access orchestrator controls from sharedData

3. **Key Design Decisions**:
   - Use VueUse's useScroll for position tracking (built-in throttling)
   - Use IntersectionObserver for trigger detection (like autoplayPlugin)
   - Use RAF for smooth scrubbing (like relationshipsPlugin)
   - Require webAnimationPlugin as optional dependency for scrub mode

4. **Scroll Progress Calculation**:
   - Parse start/end positions (support '%', 'px', named positions like 'top center')
   - Convert to pixel values
   - Calculate progress = (currentScroll - start) / (end - start)
   - Clamp to 0-1 range

â”‚ Trigger Position Parsing Strategy:

Looking at GSAP's ScrollTrigger and similar libraries, position strings have this format:
- `"top bottom"` = element's top edge at viewport's bottom edge
- `"center center"` = element's center at viewport's center
- `"80% 20%"` = element's 80% point at viewport's 20% point

Positions can be:
- Named: `top`, `center`, `bottom` (for vertical), `left`, `center`, `right` (for horizontal)
- Percentage: `"50%"`, `"80%"`
- Pixels: `"100px"`, `"200px"`

For vertical scrolling (most common):
```typescript
parsePosition("top center") => {
  element: "top",     // 0% of element height
  viewport: "center"  // 50% of viewport height
}
```

Calculation:
```typescript
// When element's top reaches viewport's center
scrollPosition = elementTop - (viewportHeight * 0.5)
```

This requires:
- getBoundingClientRect() for element position
- window.innerHeight for viewport size
- Recalculate on resize (ResizeObserver)

Alternative simpler approach for MVP:
- Just use IntersectionObserver with threshold
- Add position parsing later as enhancement

â”‚ Scrub Mode Implementation Strategy:

When scrub mode is enabled, animation progress should be synchronized with scroll progress. Looking at the research, I need to:

1. **Access the Web Animation**:
   - Get animation reference from webAnimationPlugin system
   - Check if webAnimation exists (optional dependency)
   - Access animation.currentTime property

2. **Calculate Scroll Progress**:
   ```typescript
   const progress = computed(() => {
     const current = scrollY.value
     const start = parsePosition(options.start)
     const end = parsePosition(options.end)
     return clamp((current - start) / (end - start), 0, 1)
   })
   ```

3. **Sync Animation to Scroll**:
   ```typescript
   watch(progress, (p) => {
     const animation = webAnimationSystem?.animation.value
     if (animation && options.scrub) {
       const duration = animation.effect.getTiming().duration
       animation.currentTime = duration * p
     }
   })
   ```

4. **Smooth Scrubbing**:
   If `scrub` is a number (e.g., 0.5), use that as a smoothing factor:
   ```typescript
   const smoothProgress = ref(0)
   watch(progress, (target) => {
     // Lerp towards target
     const delta = target - smoothProgress.value
     smoothProgress.value += delta * scrubSmooth
   })
   ```

5. **Pause During Scrub**:
   - Call animation.pause() when scrub mode is active
   - This prevents normal playback while scrolling
   - Resume when scroll ends if needed

”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”¤
â”‚ Edge Cases and Error Handling:

1. **Missing Dependencies**:
   - If scrub mode enabled but webAnimationPlugin not loaded
   - Solution: Log warning and disable scrub mode
   ```typescript
   if (options.scrub && !systems.has('webAnimation')) {
     console.warn('[scrollPlugin] scrub mode requires webAnimationPlugin')
     options.scrub = false
   }
   ```

2. **Invalid Scroll Container**:
   - Container element doesn't exist or not scrollable
   - Solution: Fall back to window
   ```typescript
   const container = toValue(options.container) ?? window
   ```

3. **Start > End Positions**:
   - User provides start: 1000, end: 500
   - Solution: Swap or throw error
   ```typescript
   if (startPos > endPos) {
     console.error('[scrollPlugin] start position must be before end')
     return
   }
   ```

4. **Element Not Yet Mounted**:
   - Target element ref is null during setup
   - Solution: Use watchEffect to initialize when available
   ```typescript
   watchEffect(() => {
     const el = toValue(context.target)
     if (el) setupObserver(el)
   })
   ```

5. **Resize Handling**:
   - Viewport/element dimensions change
   - Solution: Use ResizeObserver to recalculate positions
   ```typescript
   const resizeObserver = new ResizeObserver(() => {
     recalculatePositions()
   })
   ```

6. **Scroll Direction**:
   - Need to detect if scrolling up or down for callbacks
   - Solution: Use VueUse's `directions` from useScroll
   ```typescript
   const { directions } = useScroll(container)
   watch(directions.top, (scrollingUp) => {
     if (scrollingUp) onEnterBack?.()
     else onLeave?.()
   })
   ```

â”‚ Type Definitions Structure:

Looking at the existing plugin types, I need to define:

1. **ScrollPluginOptions** (user-facing API):
```typescript
interface ScrollTriggerOptions {
  element?: MaybeRefOrGetter<HTMLElement>
  threshold?: number  // 0-1 for IntersectionObserver
  start?: string | number  // 'top center', '50%', 200
  end?: string | number
  onEnter?: () => void
  onLeave?: () => void
  onEnterBack?: () => void
  onLeaveBack?: () => void
}

interface ScrollPluginOptions {
  trigger?: ScrollTriggerOptions
  scrub?: boolean | number  // true or smooth factor (0-1)
  container?: MaybeRefOrGetter<HTMLElement | Window>
  throttle?: number
  markers?: boolean  // Debug mode
}
```

2. **ScrollSystem** (plugin system return):
```typescript
interface ScrollSystem extends PluginSystem {
  // Reactive state
  position: Ref<{ x: number; y: number }>
  progress: Ref<number>  // 0-1 based on start/end
  isScrolling: Ref<boolean>
  direction: Ref<{ up: boolean; down: boolean }>
  
  // Methods
  scrollTo: (options: { x?: number; y?: number; behavior?: ScrollBehavior }) => void
  measure: () => void
  
  // Lifecycle
  pause: () => void
  resume: () => void
  cleanup: () => void
}
```

3. **Internal Types**:
```typescript
interface ParsedPosition {
  element: number  // 0-1 (percentage of element height)
  viewport: number  // 0-1 (percentage of viewport height)
}

interface ScrollState {
  inView: boolean
  progress: number
  direction: 'up' | 'down' | 'none'
}
```

â”‚ File Structure and Organization:

Based on existing plugin patterns, the scroll plugin should follow this structure:

```
src/components/vue/animations/composables/useAnimation/
â”œâ”€â”€ plugins/
â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ scrollPlugin/
â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ index.ts              # Main plugin export
â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ types.ts              # Type definitions
â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ useScrollTracking.ts  # VueUse useScroll wrapper
â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ positionParser.ts     # Parse 'top center' strings
â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ scrollScrubber.ts     # Scrub mode logic
â”‚   â””â”€â”€ index.ts                  # Re-export all plugins
â””â”€â”€ registry.ts                   # Register scroll plugin
```

**Why separate files?**:
1. `useScrollTracking.ts`: Encapsulates VueUse useScroll setup and reactive state
2. `positionParser.ts`: Pure utility for parsing position strings (testable)
3. `scrollScrubber.ts`: Scrub mode logic (can be used standalone)
4. `index.ts`: Main plugin setup and lifecycle hooks

**Main Plugin Export** (index.ts):
```typescript
export { scrollPlugin } from './scrollPlugin'
export type { ScrollPluginOptions, ScrollSystem } from './scrollPlugin/types'
```

This matches the pattern used by other plugins (CSS plugin, relationships plugin) and keeps the codebase organized.   â”‚

â”‚ Debug Markers Implementation:

When `markers: true`, the plugin should show visual indicators for scroll trigger points. This is extremely helpful during development.

**Marker Features**:
1. **Start Marker**: Shows where animation starts
2. **End Marker**: Shows where animation ends (scrub mode)
3. **Progress Bar**: Shows current scroll progress
4. **Label**: Displays trigger info (threshold, position, etc.)

**Implementation**:
```typescript
if (options.markers) {
  const markerContainer = document.createElement('div')
  markerContainer.className = 'scroll-plugin-markers'
  markerContainer.innerHTML = `
    <div class="marker start" style="top: ${startPos}px">
      <span class="label">start: ${options.start}</span>
    </div>
    <div class="marker end" style="top: ${endPos}px">
      <span class="label">end: ${options.end}</span>
    </div>
    <div class="progress-bar" style="height: ${endPos - startPos}px">
      <div class="fill" style="height: ${progress * 100}%"></div>
    </div>
  `
  document.body.appendChild(markerContainer)
  
  // Cleanup
  cleanup.push(() => markerContainer.remove())
}
```

**Marker Styles** (in design-system.css or utilities.css):
```css
.scroll-plugin-markers {
  position: fixed;
  right: 0;
  top: 0;
  z-index: 10000;
  pointer-events: none;
}

.scroll-plugin-markers .marker {
  position: absolute;
  right: 0;
  width: 100px;
  height: 2px;
  background: red;
}

.scroll-plugin-markers .label {
  font-size: 10px;
  background: rgba(255,0,0,0.8);
  color: white;
  padding: 2px 4px;
}
```

â”‚ Plugin Priority and Dependencies:

Looking at the research, existing plugin priorities are:
- responsivePlugin: 100 (runs first)
- autoplayPlugin: 40
- enterExitPlugin: 30
- webAnimationPlugin: 50
- cssAnimationPlugin: 45
- staggerPlugin: 60

**Scroll Plugin Priority**: Should be 35 (after responsive, before autoplay)

**Reasoning**:
1. Must run after responsive (100) - needs device-specific settings
2. Should run before autoplay (40) - scroll triggers can override autoplay
3. Should run before enterExit (30) - scroll is a form of viewport detection

**Dependencies**:
```typescript
{
  name: 'scroll',
  priority: 35,
  cleanupPriority: 35,
  
  // Optional: scrub mode needs webAnimation
  optionalRequires: ['webAnimation'],
  
  // Provides scroll data for other plugins
  provides: ['scroll.position', 'scroll.progress'],
  
  // Conflicts with autoplay? No - they can coexist
  // autoplay handles visibility, scroll handles position
}
```

**Integration Points**:
- Works WITH autoplay: Both can be active, scroll takes precedence
- Works WITH stagger: Scroll triggers can start staggered animations
- Requires webAnimation: Only for scrub mode
- Provides data: Other plugins can read scroll.progress from sharedData   â”‚

”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”¤
â”‚ Testing Strategy:

The scroll plugin needs comprehensive tests to ensure reliability:

**Unit Tests** (scrollPlugin.test.ts):
1. **Position Parser Tests**:
   - Parse named positions: 'top center' â†’ { element: 0, viewport: 0.5 }
   - Parse percentages: '50% 80%' â†’ { element: 0.5, viewport: 0.8 }
   - Parse pixels: '100px 200px' â†’ pixel values
   - Handle invalid inputs gracefully

2. **Progress Calculation Tests**:
   - Calculate 0-1 progress from scroll position
   - Clamp values outside range
   - Handle start > end error case
   - Test with different container sizes

3. **Trigger Detection Tests**:
   - Detect enter/leave events
   - Track scroll direction for enterBack/leaveBack
   - Threshold-based triggering
   - Multiple threshold support

**Integration Tests** (with mock Web Animation API):
1. **Scrub Mode**:
   - Animation.currentTime updates with scroll
   - Smooth scrubbing with lerp factor
   - Pause animation during scrub
   - Resume after scroll ends

2. **Plugin Lifecycle**:
   - Setup creates scroll tracking
   - Watchers register correctly
   - Cleanup removes observers
   - No memory leaks

**E2E Tests** (with Playwright):
1. Scroll page and verify animation triggers
2. Scrub mode syncs animation to scroll
3. Markers appear in debug mode
4. Works with different scroll containers

This ensures the plugin is production-ready.   â”‚

â”‚ Performance Optimization Strategies:

Scroll events can fire hundreds of times per second, so performance is critical:

1. **Throttling Strategy**:
   - Use VueUse's built-in throttle (default: 0ms = RAF-based)
   - For scrub mode: Use RAF for 60fps updates
   - For trigger mode: Use IntersectionObserver (no scroll events!)

2. **Avoid Layout Thrashing**:
   ```typescript
   // âŒ BAD: Multiple reads/writes
   element.style.transform = `translateY(${scrollY}px)` // Write
   const height = element.offsetHeight // Read (forces reflow)
   
   // âœ… GOOD: Batch reads, then batch writes
   const positions = elements.map(el => el.getBoundingClientRect()) // Batch reads
   positions.forEach((pos, i) => {
     elements[i].style.transform = `translateY(${pos.y}px)` // Batch writes
   })
   ```

3. **Use will-change for GPU Acceleration**:
   ```css
   .scroll-animated {
     will-change: transform;
   }
   ```

4. **Passive Event Listeners**:
   - VueUse handles this automatically
   - But if manual: `{ passive: true }` for scroll events

5. **Debounce Resize Calculations**:
   ```typescript
   const debouncedRecalc = useDebounceFn(() => {
     recalculatePositions()
   }, 150)
   
   resizeObserver = new ResizeObserver(debouncedRecalc)
   ```

6. **Lazy Observer Creation**:
   - Only create IntersectionObserver when element is in DOM
   - Use watchEffect to delay until element exists

7. **Memory Management**:
   - Clean up all observers in cleanup()
   - Remove event listeners
   - Clear references to prevent memory leaks

These optimizations ensure smooth 60fps performance even with multiple scroll-triggered animations.   â”‚

â”‚ API Expansions - What did I miss?

Looking at my original API design and comparing with GSAP ScrollTrigger and similar libraries, I should add:

1. **Pin/Sticky Behavior**:
   ```typescript
   scroll: {
     pin?: boolean | HTMLElement,  // Pin element during scroll range
     pinSpacing?: boolean,          // Add spacing when pinned
     anticipatePin?: number         // Start pinning early
   }
   ```

2. **Snap Points**:
   ```typescript
   scroll: {
     snap?: {
       snapTo: number | number[] | 'labels',  // Snap to positions
       duration: number,                       // Snap animation duration
       delay: number,                          // Delay before snap
       ease: string                            // Snap easing
     }
   }
   ```

3. **Horizontal Scrolling**:
   ```typescript
   scroll: {
     horizontal?: boolean,  // Track horizontal scroll instead
     axis?: 'x' | 'y' | 'both'  // Which axis to track
   }
   ```

4. **Batch Callbacks**:
   ```typescript
   scroll: {
     onUpdate?: (self: ScrollState) => void,  // Every scroll update
     onToggle?: (self: ScrollState) => void,  // When active state changes
     onRefresh?: () => void                    // When positions recalculated
   }
   ```

5. **Advanced Triggers**:
   ```typescript
   scroll: {
     toggleActions?: string,  // 'play pause resume reset'
     fastScrollEnd?: boolean, // Detect fast scroll and skip to end
     preventOverlaps?: boolean // Prevent overlapping triggers
   }
   ```

However, for MVP, I should focus on core features:
- Basic trigger (IntersectionObserver-based)
- Scrub mode (progress-linked animation)
- Scroll position tracking
- Callbacks (onEnter, onLeave, etc.)

Advanced features (pin, snap, horizontal) can be added in v2.   â”‚

â”‚ Revised Final API Design:

After all the analysis, here's the refined API that balances features with simplicity:

```typescript
// Usage in useAnimation
const { play, scroll } = useAnimation(elementRef, {
  animation: { preset: 'fadeIn', duration: 1000 },
  
  scroll: {
    // TRIGGER MODE: When to activate animation
    trigger?: {
      element?: HTMLElement,      // Element to observe (default: target)
      threshold?: number,          // IntersectionObserver threshold (0-1)
      start?: string | number,     // 'top center', '50%', 200px
      end?: string | number,       // For scrub mode range
      rootMargin?: string,         // IntersectionObserver rootMargin
      
      // Callbacks
      onEnter?: () => void,        // Scrolling down, enters trigger
      onLeave?: () => void,        // Scrolling down, leaves trigger
      onEnterBack?: () => void,    // Scrolling up, enters trigger
      onLeaveBack?: () => void,    // Scrolling up, leaves trigger
    },
    
    // SCRUB MODE: Sync animation to scroll
    scrub?: boolean | number,      // true or smooth factor (0-1)
    
    // CONTAINER
    container?: HTMLElement | Window,
    
    // PERFORMANCE
    throttle?: number,             // Throttle scroll events (ms)
    
    // CALLBACKS
    onUpdate?: (progress: number) => void,  // Every scroll update
    onRefresh?: () => void,                  // When recalculated
    
    // DEBUG
    markers?: boolean,             // Show visual debug markers
  }
})

// Exposed API
scroll.position     // Ref<{ x: number, y: number }>
scroll.progress     // Ref<number> (0-1)
scroll.isScrolling  // Ref<boolean>
scroll.direction    // Ref<{ up: boolean, down: boolean }>
scroll.scrollTo({ y: 100, behavior: 'smooth' })
scroll.refresh()    // Recalculate positions
```

This API:
- âœ… Follows existing plugin patterns
- âœ… Supports both trigger and scrub modes
- âœ… Integrates with VueUse useScroll
- âœ… Provides callbacks for all scroll events
- âœ… Exposes scroll state for external use
- âœ… Has debug mode for development
- âœ… Performant (IntersectionObserver + RAF)

â”‚ Implementation Steps - Detailed Breakdown:

**Phase 1: Core Infrastructure** (Day 1-2)
1. Create file structure:
   - `scrollPlugin/index.ts` - Main plugin
   - `scrollPlugin/types.ts` - Type definitions
   - `scrollPlugin/useScrollTracking.ts` - VueUse wrapper
   - `scrollPlugin/utils.ts` - Helper functions

2. Implement type definitions:
   - ScrollPluginOptions interface
   - ScrollSystem interface
   - ScrollTriggerOptions interface
   - Internal types (ParsedPosition, ScrollState)

3. Register plugin in registry:
   - Add to globalRegistry
   - Set priority: 35
   - Set optionalRequires: ['webAnimation']

**Phase 2: Scroll Tracking** (Day 2-3)
1. Implement useScrollTracking.ts:
   - Wrap VueUse useScroll
   - Create reactive position refs
   - Calculate progress (0-1)
   - Track direction (up/down)

2. Setup scroll container handling:
   - Support window or HTMLElement
   - Handle container ref changes
   - Auto-fallback to window

**Phase 3: Trigger Mode** (Day 3-4)
1. Implement IntersectionObserver setup:
   - Parse threshold from options
   - Create observer for target element
   - Track visibility state

2. Implement callbacks:
   - Detect scroll direction
   - Call onEnter/onLeave appropriately
   - Call onEnterBack/onLeaveBack based on direction
   - Integration with play()/pause() from orchestrator

**Phase 4: Scrub Mode** (Day 4-5)
1. Implement animation scrubbing:
   - Get animation from webAnimationPlugin
   - Watch scroll progress
   - Update animation.currentTime
   - Pause animation during scrub

2. Implement smooth scrubbing:
   - Add lerp for smooth factor
   - Use RAF for 60fps updates
   - Handle edge cases (no animation, etc.)

**Phase 5: Position Parsing** (Day 5-6)
1. Implement position parser:
   - Parse named positions ('top', 'center', 'bottom')
   - Parse percentages ('50%', '80%')
   - Parse pixels ('100px', '200px')
   - Calculate actual scroll positions

2. Handle resize:
   - Add ResizeObserver
   - Recalculate on resize
   - Debounce recalculations

**Phase 6: Debug Markers** (Day 6)
1. Implement marker rendering:
   - Create marker DOM elements
   - Position at start/end points
   - Show progress bar
   - Add labels

2. Style markers:
   - Add CSS to utilities.css
   - Make markers responsive
   - Only in dev mode

**Phase 7: Testing** (Day 7-8)
1. Unit tests
2. Integration tests
3. E2E tests with Playwright

This gives a clear 7-8 day implementation timeline.   â”‚

â”‚ Code Implementation Example - setup() method:

Let me draft the actual implementation to ensure it's feasible:

```typescript
export const scrollPlugin: AnimationPlugin<ScrollPluginOptions, ScrollSystem> = {
  name: 'scroll',
  version: '1.0.0',
  priority: 35,
  optionsKey: 'scroll',
  optionalRequires: ['webAnimation'],
  provides: ['scroll.position', 'scroll.progress', 'scroll.direction'],
  
  setup(context, options) {
    const target = toValue(context.target)
    const container = toValue(options.container) ?? window
    
    // 1. Initialize VueUse scroll tracking
    const { x, y, isScrolling, directions } = useScroll(container, {
      throttle: options.throttle ?? 0,
      idle: 200,
      behavior: 'smooth'
    })
    
    // 2. Calculate scroll progress (0-1)
    const scrollProgress = computed(() => {
      if (!options.trigger?.start || !options.trigger?.end) return 0
      
      const startPos = parseScrollPosition(options.trigger.start, target, container)
      const endPos = parseScrollPosition(options.trigger.end, target, container)
      const current = y.value
      
      return Math.max(0, Math.min(1, (current - startPos) / (endPos - startPos)))
    })
    
    // 3. Store in sharedData for other plugins
    context.sharedData.set('scroll.position', { x, y })
    context.sharedData.set('scroll.progress', scrollProgress)
    context.sharedData.set('scroll.direction', directions)
    
    // 4. Create scroll system
    const system: ScrollSystem = {
      position: computed(() => ({ x: x.value, y: y.value })),
      progress: scrollProgress,
      isScrolling,
      direction: computed(() => ({ 
        up: directions.top, 
        down: directions.bottom 
      })),
      
      scrollTo: (opts) => {
        if (opts.y !== undefined) y.value = opts.y
        if (opts.x !== undefined) x.value = opts.x
      },
      
      refresh: () => {
        // Recalculate positions
        scrollProgress.value // Triggers recomputation
      },
      
      cleanup: () => {
        // VueUse handles cleanup automatically
      }
    }
    
    context.sharedData.set('scroll.system', system)
    return system
  }
}
```

This looks solid and follows the pattern from other plugins. The structure is clean and testable.

â”‚ Code Implementation Example - registerWatchers() method:

This is where the scroll plugin connects with the orchestrator to trigger animations:

```typescript
registerWatchers(context) {
  const watchers: WatchStopHandle[] = []
  const system = context.sharedData.get('scroll.system') as ScrollSystem
  const play = context.sharedData.get('orchestrator.play')
  const pause = context.sharedData.get('orchestrator.pause')
  const options = context.options.scroll as ScrollPluginOptions
  
  // 1. TRIGGER MODE: Play/pause based on visibility
  if (options.trigger) {
    let isInView = false
    let lastDirection: 'up' | 'down' = 'down'
    
    // Create IntersectionObserver
    const observer = new IntersectionObserver((entries) => {
      entries.forEach((entry) => {
        const wasInView = isInView
        isInView = entry.isIntersecting
        const currentDirection = system.direction.value.down ? 'down' : 'up'
        
        if (isInView && !wasInView) {
          // Entering
          if (currentDirection === 'down') {
            options.trigger?.onEnter?.()
            play?.()
          } else {
            options.trigger?.onEnterBack?.()
            play?.()
          }
        } else if (!isInView && wasInView) {
          // Leaving
          if (currentDirection === 'down') {
            options.trigger?.onLeave?.()
            if (!options.scrub) pause?.()
          } else {
            options.trigger?.onLeaveBack?.()
            if (!options.scrub) pause?.()
          }
        }
        
        lastDirection = currentDirection
      })
    }, { threshold: options.trigger.threshold ?? 0.25 })
    
    const target = toValue(context.target)
    if (target) observer.observe(target)
    
    watchers.push(() => observer.disconnect())
  }
  
  // 2. SCRUB MODE: Sync animation to scroll
  if (options.scrub) {
    const webAnimationSystem = context.sharedData.get('webAnimation.system')
    
    if (webAnimationSystem) {
      const stopProgressWatch = watch(system.progress, (progress) => {
        const animation = webAnimationSystem.animation?.value
        if (animation) {
          const duration = animation.effect?.getTiming().duration as number
          animation.currentTime = duration * progress
          
          // Pause animation so it doesn't auto-play
          if (animation.playState === 'running') {
            animation.pause()
          }
        }
      })
      
      watchers.push(stopProgressWatch)
    } else {
      console.warn('[scrollPlugin] scrub mode requires webAnimationPlugin')
    }
  }
  
  // 3. onUpdate callback
  if (options.onUpdate) {
    const stopUpdateWatch = watch(system.progress, (progress) => {
      options.onUpdate?.(progress)
    })
    watchers.push(stopUpdateWatch)
  }
  
  return watchers
}
```

This implementation:
- âœ… Uses IntersectionObserver for trigger mode (performant)
- âœ… Detects scroll direction for proper callbacks
- âœ… Syncs animation.currentTime in scrub mode
- âœ… Pauses animation during scrub
- âœ… Handles missing dependencies gracefully
- âœ… Returns cleanup functions

Perfect pattern match with existing plugins!

â”‚ Documentation and Examples:

The scroll plugin needs comprehensive documentation for developers:

**1. API Reference Documentation**:
```markdown
# Scroll Plugin

## Installation
The scroll plugin is built-in to useAnimation.

## Basic Usage

### Trigger Mode
```typescript
useAnimation(elementRef, {
  animation: { preset: 'fadeIn' },
  scroll: {
    trigger: {
      threshold: 0.5,
      onEnter: () => console.log('Entered'),
      onLeave: () => console.log('Left')
    }
  }
})
```

### Scrub Mode
```typescript
useAnimation(elementRef, {
  animation: { preset: 'fadeIn', duration: 1000 },
  scroll: {
    trigger: { start: 'top bottom', end: 'bottom top' },
    scrub: true  // Sync animation to scroll
  }
})
```
```

**2. Example Components**:
Create example components showing:
- Scroll-triggered fade in
- Parallax effect with scrub
- Scroll progress indicator
- Staggered list reveal
- Horizontal scroll integration

**3. Recipe Documentation**:
Add to `ANIMATION_RECIPES.md`:
- How to create scroll-triggered animations
- How to implement parallax scrolling
- How to build scroll progress bars
- How to handle multiple scroll triggers

**4. TypeScript Definitions**:
Export all types for developer autocomplete:
```typescript
export type { 
  ScrollPluginOptions,
  ScrollSystem,
  ScrollTriggerOptions
}
```

This ensures developers can use the plugin effectively.

â”‚ Final Verification and Edge Cases:

Before presenting the plan, let me verify I haven't missed any critical edge cases:

**1. SSR Compatibility**:
- IntersectionObserver only exists in browser
- Need `if (typeof window !== 'undefined')` checks
- VueUse handles this automatically with `useScroll`

**2. Hot Module Replacement**:
- Cleanup observers on component unmount
- Re-register on hot reload
- Registry handles this automatically

**3. Multiple Scroll Containers**:
- Support nested scrollable divs
- Each animation can have different container
- VueUse supports this out of the box

**4. Dynamic Elements**:
- Target element ref changes
- Use watchEffect to re-observe
- Clean up old observers

**5. Animation Already Playing**:
- Don't interrupt if animation is mid-play
- Check animation state before scrubbing
- Respect user-initiated plays

**6. Browser Compatibility**:
- IntersectionObserver: Chrome 51+, Firefox 55+, Safari 12.1+
- Web Animations API: Chrome 36+, Firefox 48+, Safari 13.1+
- Provide polyfill recommendations in docs

**7. Memory Leaks**:
- Disconnect observers in cleanup
- Remove watchers
- Clear sharedData references

â”‚ Implementation Priority and MVP Scope:

Given the comprehensive design, I need to define what's in scope for the MVP vs future enhancements:

**MVP (v1.0.0) - Core Features**:
âœ… Trigger mode with IntersectionObserver
âœ… Basic threshold-based triggering
âœ… Scrub mode (sync animation to scroll)
âœ… VueUse useScroll integration
âœ… Callbacks (onEnter, onLeave, onEnterBack, onLeaveBack)
âœ… Scroll position/progress tracking
âœ… Direction detection
âœ… Basic error handling
âœ… TypeScript types
âœ… Core tests

**Future Enhancements (v1.1.0+)**:
- Advanced position parsing ('top center', 'bottom top')
- Debug markers
- Pin/sticky behavior
- Snap points
- Horizontal scrolling support
- Smooth scrubbing (lerp factor)
- Performance monitoring
- E2E tests

**MVP Timeline**: 3-4 days
**Full Implementation**: 7-8 days

Starting with MVP gets the core functionality working quickly, then we can iterate based on real usage feedback.

- VueUse's useScroll for scroll position tracking
- IntersectionObserver for trigger detection (performant, no scroll events)
- Web Animations API for scrub mode (currentTime manipulation)
- RAF coordination for smooth updates

**API Design** (refined):
```typescript
scroll: {
  trigger?: {
    threshold?: number,
    onEnter/onLeave/onEnterBack/onLeaveBack?: () => void
  },
  scrub?: boolean | number,
  container?: HTMLElement | Window,
  throttle?: number,
  onUpdate?: (progress) => void,
  markers?: boolean
}
```

**MVP Features**: Trigger mode, scrub mode, callbacks, scroll tracking
**Future Features**: Advanced position parsing, debug markers, pin/sticky, snap points

**Implementation**: 7 phases over 7-8 days (or 3-4 days for MVP only)

**Files to Create**:
- scrollPlugin/index.ts (main plugin)
- scrollPlugin/types.ts (TypeScript definitions)
- scrollPlugin/useScrollTracking.ts (VueUse wrapper)
- scrollPlugin/utils.ts (helpers)

**Integration**: Priority 35, optionalRequires: ['webAnimation'], provides scroll data

I'm ready to present the complete plan now.
